1935.04.19

National Government Holds Ceremony Commemorating the Founding of the Capital in Nanjing; Chairman Lin Delivers Commemorative Speech 1

(Nanjing) This morning at 10:00 a.m. on the 18th, the National Government held a ceremony commemorating the eighth anniversary of the founding of the capital in Nanjing. Those present included Ju Zheng, Yu Youren, Dai Chuanxian, Tang Shengzhi, Chen Diaoyuan, Chen Shaokuan, Bai Wenwei, Zhu Jiahua, Chen Qicai, Chen Shuren, Wang Yongbin, Chen Xunyong, Cao Haosen, Lin Xiang, Chu Minyi, Chen Daqi, Ma Chaojun, Chen Zhuo, Lü Chao, Wei Huai, and others, as well as senior officers from various ministries and commissions, totaling approximately 800 people. After music was played and rituals were performed, Chairman Lin delivered a speech, briefly stating that today marks the eighth anniversary of the founding of the capital in Nanjing. Nanjing was once prosperous, but after the devastating destruction by Hong and Yang, the fields were barren, and traces of this still remain. When we established the capital here, we had to make do with what we had. After eight years of arduous efforts, new buildings are now visible everywhere. Furthermore, the construction of affordable housing areas is also actively underway. Nanjing is the capital of our country and is of great international importance. Therefore, all construction should be magnificent and dignified, fully in line with Eastern culture, in order to show a positive image to foreigners. In terms of science, libraries, medical schools, and the like should be vigorously established in the capital. In addition, the scenic beauty of the Qinhuai River should be preserved in its natural state and utilized with artificial and scientific methods to create a scenic area for the residents. The population of Nanjing has already increased to 800,000, and the construction needed is truly vast. Sun Yat-sen advocated establishing the capital in Nanjing because Beiping was corrupt and outdated. He hopes that all comrades will uphold Sun Yat-sen's legacy, work together, and ensure that the new construction of the capital continues to progress. After the speech, music was played, and the ceremony concluded. The entire group went to the front courtyard inside the main gate for a group photo, after which refreshments were served, and the meeting adjourned. The staff of the National Government's Civil Affairs, Accounting, and Military Affairs departments changed the gathering place and had lunch at various locations due to the rain to celebrate. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 18th)

Central Standing Committee Meeting 2

(Nanjing) The Central Committee held its 167th Standing Committee meeting this morning, with over twenty people including Wang Zhaoming, Sun Ke, Ye Chucang, Ju Zheng, Chu Minyi, Chen Lifu, Bai Wenwei, and Dai Chuanxian attending. Sun Ke chaired the meeting. (1) Amendments were made to Articles 6, 15, and 17 of the Organizational Regulations of the Central People's Movement Guidance Committee. (2) The Organization Outline and Detailed Rules of Procedure of the Revolutionary Debt Investigation Committee were approved for record. (3) Li Haiyun and Huang Dingzhi were additionally appointed as members of the Revolutionary Debt Investigation Committee. (4) The relocation of the tombs of the Guangdong Army martyrs who died in the founding of the country at Mochou Lake in Nanjing to the Martyrs' Cemetery was handled by the Cemetery Preparatory Committee. (5) Wang Zhaoming, Ye Chucang, and Chen Xieren were additionally appointed as members of the Liao Zhongkai Funeral Preparatory Office, with Wang Zhaoming as the convener. (6) Regarding the order of filling vacancies for Central Party Headquarters staff who have passed the political work examination, it was resolved that they should be given priority in employment in accordance with special laws, and the general method of filling vacancies should not apply. However, promotions, transfers, performance evaluations, etc., after employment should still be handled in accordance with ordinary laws. (7) Dai Chuanxian was recommended to report at the Central Memorial Week next Monday. (8) Other routine cases. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 18th)

Legislative Yuan Revises Accountants Law, Loosens Restrictions on Accountants Holding Concurrent Positions, Passes Shandong's General Budget for the 23rd Year 3

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan held its 13th meeting at 2:00 p.m. on the 18th, with 68 people, including Wei Tingsheng, in attendance. Sun Ke chaired the meeting, and Liang Hancao served as Secretary-General. After reading the report items, the revised Accountants Law was reviewed and passed. Since the law was promulgated and implemented by the National Government, the restrictions on accountants holding concurrent positions were quite strict, and the business of accountants in various regions was greatly affected. Requests were made to loosen the restrictions. In order to facilitate accountants, the authorities decided to make revisions, limiting accountants only from serving as managers, directors, or supervisors of industrial and commercial enterprises. Furthermore, in order to maintain the credibility of accountants, it was stipulated that they should not hold positions as civil servants. Other articles, apart from modifications to the wording, did not have major changes in content. In addition, the general budget for local ordinary revenue and expenditure of Shandong Province for the 23rd year was passed, but the province was instructed that the proportion of expenses such as education should be increased in the future. Finally, a major case regarding finance was passed. The meeting adjourned at 5:30 p.m. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 18th)

Control Yuan Meeting 4

(Nanjing) At the Control Yuan's administrative meeting on the 18th, the Secretariat reported that from the establishment of the Control Yuan in February of the 20th year to March of this year, a total of 465 impeachment and transfer cases had been filed. Among them, 159 cases were resolved with disciplinary actions by the disciplinary organs, 34 cases were resolved without disciplinary actions, and 272 cases had not yet been processed by the disciplinary organs. Next, the impeachment case proposed by Control Committee member Zhu Leizhang was discussed. It was proposed that a notice of rapid relief measures should be attached to the case, notifying the主管長官 (responsible superior) to suspend the impeached person from his position and place him under surveillance first, and at the same time notify the court to investigate the case. It was resolved to hand it over to Liu Eqing and ten others for review. In addition, the Control Yuan has set the date for the inauguration of the inspectors on the 29th of this month, and has telegraphed to urge all inspectors to come to Nanjing for training before the inauguration. (Special dispatch from the 18th)

Guizhou剿匪 Army Continuously Captures Dingfan and Guangshun 5

Guiyang: Our army, the Sun Column, has been fiercely suppressing the bandit Pseudo-135th Army Corps in the Huangni Shao Guanyin Mountain area for several days, capturing many prisoners. Starting from the 10th, they have been tailing the fleeing remnants of the bandits, pursuing them fiercely towards the Dingfan and Tonggupo areas of Zhongbai. After many fierce battles, over 3,000 bandits were scattered along the way. The Sun Column recovered Dingfan city on the 11th and Guangshun city on the 13th. The remnants of the bandits fled towards Ziyun. It is estimated that the bandits suffered over 4,000 casualties, with over 2,000 captured. Chiang Kai-shek, cherishing the loyalty and hard work of the generals and soldiers for the Party and the country, specially awarded 30,000 yuan and instructed subordinates to inform them. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 18th)

(Changsha) Wang Jialie telegraphed that the remnants of Zhu De and Mao Zedong's forces were attempting to enter Yunnan and were fleeing towards Anzhen, Pingchangba, and Mugang. They have been fiercely suppressed by our army for days, suffering thousands of casualties. There are no traces of bandits in Dingfan, Datang, or Longli. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 18th)

Guo Siyan Appointed Commander of the Guiyang Garrison 6

(Hankou) Chiang Kai-shek appointed Guo Siyan as the Commander of the Guiyang Garrison in Guiyang and telegraphed the Nanjing Military Commission to request formal appointment from the National Government. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 18th)

Confirmation of Zhu De's Death in Battle 7

Guiyang: Regarding the death of bandit leader Zhu De, it has now been reconfirmed that Wang Zhengxiang, a local villager from Shuitian Shou Township in Guanyang County, was captured by bandits while going to Xinchang and was forced to carry corpses through places such as Kelong Yangbao and Baini. He clearly heard the bandits saying, "Mr. Zhu (the bandits' term for him) died in battle at Zhujie Mountain this time." At the time, a bandit in a sedan saw Mr. Zhu's death and cried loudly. After much persuasion from several bandit officers, he stopped and immediately ordered the corpse to be wrapped in red silk and sent many soldiers to protect it. Along the way, a foul odor was heard. According to the coolies who carried the corpse, whenever the Red bandits stopped to rest, they would offer food, burn incense, and pay their respects. They would also silently pray, "Committee Member Zhu, bless us to break through Guizhou and send you back." They personally saw the silk inside the head of the corpse, and because of the shaking during transport, the lower half of the right ear was rubbed off, revealing the beard of a man of Ren Dan (probably a man who has experience). The face was swollen, and it was impossible to tell whether he was fat or thin. When a Red bandit saw the corpse's ear exposed, he beat the coolies violently and tied them with ropes. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 17th)

Dispute Between Military and Civilians Over Muli Gold Mine in Southern Sichuan; Three Representatives Arrive in Nanjing to Petition for Relief 8

(Nanjing) The Muli Jiusuo Tusi (chieftain) in Southern Sichuan is located at the junction of Sichuan, Yunnan, and Xikang and has always been under the jurisdiction of Yanyuan County in Sichuan Province. Recently, due to the issue of the Longda Gold Mine in Muli, a dispute arose with the troops of Liu Wenhui. Therefore, three representatives were specially sent to Nanjing to petition: Yue Wuye Da (representative of the three major monasteries in Muli), Xi Luo Jixiang (monastery representative), and Song Nuo Jize (representative of the Jiusuo people). They arrived yesterday. According to the representatives, the Tusi areas of Jiusuo in Muli have been at peace for over 300 years since the Kangxi period of the Qing Dynasty. The local people are law-abiding and loyal. However, after Liu Wenhui's troops retreated to Ya'an in the 21st year, Ningyuan's eight counties were placed under their garrison. Because the troops took over the Longda Gold Mine, the mining performance was poor, and disputes arose with the Tusi, eventually leading to the death of the Tusi, Xiang Ci Cheng Zha Ba, and the imprisonment of the young Tusi, Zha Ba Song Dian, who has not yet been released. The Jiusuo people made a special decision through a general meeting to send representatives to Nanjing to petition, traveling over 10,000 li via Shanghai to Nanjing. They will soon petition the Executive Yuan and the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission of the National Government, requesting relief. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 18th)

Special Police Force Can Only Depart After Security Commander is Confirmed; Zhang Yantian and Zhang Qingyu Visit Takahashi; Counties in the Luan-Yu Area Discuss Summer Defense 9

(Tianjin) The departure of the newly compiled Special Police 1st and 2nd Regiments of the War Zone for their eastward shift of defense on the 18th did not materialize. The Beining and Jinpu Railway Bureaus had prepared vehicles, which were withdrawn from Yangcun and Cangxian on the night of the 17th. According to sources, the delay in the special police shift is still due to the unresolved issue of the security commander. Before the command authority is determined, it is difficult to provide aid for the time being. It is expected that after Yin Tong returns from Japan, the Clearing Committee will be reconvened to decide everything and a military ruling body will be organized, following the example of the administrative commissioners of Henan, Jiangsu, and Anhui provinces concurrently serving as security commanders. (Special dispatch from the 18th)

(Tianjin) Liu Zuozhou, the commander of the 1st Security Regiment of the War Zone, arrived in Tangshan from Wanxian on the afternoon of the 17th to meet with Commissioner Tao Shangming. Because they were waiting for Zhu Shiqin, the commissioner of the Clearing Committee, to come for inspection, the troops were specially stationed in Tangshan to wait. The security and militia groups in the Ao-Yu area will implement a joint defense system. When any security team encounters bandit alarms, they will dispatch troops to block and suppress them, regardless of defense boundaries. Tao Shangming took the opportunity of Liu Zuozhou's visit to Tangshan and planned to convene Zhao Lei, Feng Shoupeng, and others on the 19th to exchange views together. (Special dispatch from the 18th)

(Beiping) Zhang Yantian and Zhang Qingyu, the commanders of the War Zone Security Corps, came to Peiping to pay respects to He Yingqin and Wang Kemin and reported on the inspection and organization of the new security team. This morning, still guided by Yin Rugeng, they visited Takahashi at the Japanese Embassy for about an hour. It was decided that they would leave Peiping immediately to return to their defense. (Special dispatch from the 18th)

(Beiping) The War Zone Clearing Committee had previously planned to send three committee members, including Zhu Shiqin, to various places in the Luan-Yu area to inspect the security teams of Liu Zuozhou, Zhao Lei, and others. It is heard that Zhu and others will leave Peiping in the coming days and will first go to Tangshan and then to Ao Zhou and other places. Regarding the reorganization of the War Zone Security Team, it is heard that it has been decided to reorganize Feng Shoupeng's unit first. Once Feng's unit is also reorganized, the new security team can enter. The Hebei Provincial Government has instructed Zhang Qingyu, Zhang Yantian, and others stationed in Caicun and other places in Cangzhou to prepare everything. (Special dispatch from the 18th)

(Beiping) The Ao-Yu Regional Office is planning summer joint defense measures for the counties. It will convene the security team leaders Liu Zuozhou, Zhao Lei, and Feng Shoupeng in the coming days to discuss them, and then they can be implemented. It is heard that the content of the measures is that all security teams and militias will be stationed in various villages and towns according to the designated locations. In the event of a bandit alarm, they will jointly suppress them. (Special dispatch from the 18th)

(Beiping) According to Tangshan, the administrative conference of the Wan-Yu area will be held on May 10th after the newly compiled security team of the war zone enters. The Linyu Regional Office has notified the counties under its jurisdiction to prepare proposals. At that time, the county magistrates of nine counties, including Linyu, Funing, etc., and the heads of the two special public security bureaus can attend the conference in Tangshan. Tao Shangming will also depart to inspect the administrative situation in various counties before the meeting. (Special dispatch from the 18th)

(Beiping) Liu Zuozhou, the commander of the 1st Security Regiment of the War Zone, convened a meeting of leaders from all walks of life in Luan County at the headquarters on the 16th of this month to discuss issues such as the organization of local militias and local security. Liu visited Tao Shangming in Tangshan on the 17th from Ao to report on the recent situation of the team and discuss issues such as the exchange of defense and local security after the new security team enters. Liu, because the inspection commissioner of the War Zone Clearing Committee will soon arrive in Tangshan and will discuss summer defense issues with Zhao Lei, Feng Shoupeng, and others, will stay for three or four days before returning to Luan. Liu said that the issue of the new security team entering the war zone has been agreed upon by all parties, but there is no definite date yet. It has been decided that this unit and the units of Zhao Lei and Feng Shoupeng will remain in their original defenses and will not be transferred for the time being. (Special dispatch from the 18th)

Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteers Surround Huadian Gold Mine 10

(Tianjin) According to Harbin, over 200 anti-Japanese volunteers from the Taiping unit surrounded the Yijin Gold Mine of the Datong Colonial Production Company in Huadian County on the 14th and engaged in fierce battles with the garrison for several hours. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 18th)

Luan-Yu Administrative Conference Postponed to May 10th 11

(Tianjin) The administrative conference of the Luan-Yu Administrative Region has been postponed to May 10th. The participants are the nine county magistrates and the two public security bureau chiefs. The important agenda item is the joint defense of the counties in summer. Recently, the Ao-Yu Commissioner's Office has notified the county magistrates to prepare proposals. (Special dispatch from the 18th)

Bandits in Pianshiyu Flee Outside the Pass 12

(Beiping) The bandits who previously fled to Pianshiyu in Zunhua have been actively attacked by the local security team and militia and have now fled outside the pass. To prevent their return, strict precautions have been taken. (Special dispatch from the 18th)

(Beiping) After the illegal militia of Wang Jizong in Yutian was resolved, there are remnants of bandits fleeing everywhere. The remnants of this unit are all former troops of Liu Guitang. Liu himself is in Tianjin, directing remotely. According to a certain foreign doctor, he has been very ill recently and is bedridden. (Special dispatch from the 18th)

Various Ministries and Commissions Review Rules for Issuing Passports 13

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan, considering that various administrative organs issue passports without restrictions, which can easily lead to malpractices, has recently drafted rules for administrative organs to issue passports in order to unify restrictions. At 3:00 p.m. on the 18th, the military, political, internal affairs, transportation, railway, Mongolian and Tibetan affairs, overseas Chinese affairs, and prohibition of marriage ministries and commissions were convened to review the rules. Many opinions were expressed. After sorting them out, they will be submitted to the Yuan Council for discussion. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 18th)

Date for Abolition of Transit Tax Scheduled for June 1st 14

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance's request to abolish the transit tax has been approved by the Central Government and will be formally implemented on June 1st. An order will be issued to stop collecting the tax immediately. (Special dispatch from the 18th)

Labor Representative Arrives in Nanjing to Participate in the International Labour Conference 15

(Nanjing) The labor representative of our country attending the 19th International Labour Conference has been appointed as Wang Jinxia, a dock worker from Hankou. He arrived in Nanjing from Hankou on the 18th to prepare to go abroad at the end of the month. Wang said that the labor issue is a matter of equality for working people in terms of life and culture, as well as a matter of belief and responsibility to the country and nation. The needs of workers in our country today focus particularly on the awakening of national consciousness and the training of life skills. The International Labour Conference is a progressive way to promote international labor friendship. I plan to have two proposals. One is to prevent dumping policies to protect the lives of workers and the benefits they are entitled to. Dumping is enough to cause international moral problems and is unreasonable from a social point of view. Our country's industry and workers suffer the most from this impact, so I especially request discussion. The other case is still under consideration. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 18th)

Xiamen Chamber of Commerce Discusses Silver Export Issue; Sends Letter to Customs Temporarily Prohibiting Silver Exports 16

(Xiamen) At 4:00 p.m. on the 18th, the Xiamen Chamber of Commerce convened an emergency meeting of all directors and supervisors of various banks and trade associations to address the recent large-scale export of silver. The presidents of seven banks, including the Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Zhongnan Bank, Industrial Bank, Zhongxing Bank, Xinhua Bank, and Guohua Bank, as well as representatives from various trade associations such as money shops, and all directors and supervisors of the Chamber of Commerce attended. After discussion, the following resolutions were made: (1) Submit a letter to the municipal government and the customs, requesting a temporary ban on silver exports from today onwards, with no restrictions on those entering and leaving Zhangzhou and Quanzhou inland. (2) The Chamber of Commerce will organize a disciplinary team to detain those who violate the resolution and transport silver, and cooperate with the police to maintain financial stability. (Special dispatch from the 18th)

(Xiamen) The city has exported more than 1.3 million yuan of silver in recent days, not counting smuggling. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 17th)

Three Banks in Tianjin Discuss Silver Issue 17

(Tianjin) The Bank of China, Bank of Communications, and Central Bank in Tianjin held a meeting at the Central Bank at 4:30 p.m. on the 18th to discuss the issue of preventing silver from overflowing from Tianjin. It is planned to send a letter to foreign banks in Tianjin to cooperate in prevention. Recently, unscrupulous merchants have smuggled silver out of Tianjin, carrying it on civilian ships to Yuguan and then transporting it to Korea via the pseudo-Fengshan Road, amounting to tens of thousands of gold per day. The city's silver reserves were 60 million, but now they are less than 32 million. Silver has disappeared in rural markets, and the economy is in a state of panic. (Special dispatch from the 18th)

Ministry of Railways Plans to Extend Longhai Railway 18

(Nanjing) After the Longhai Railway reached Xi'an, Zeng Zhongming of the Ministry of Railways is planning extension measures and has ordered Hong Guantao, the director of the Engineering Bureau, to come to Nanjing for negotiations. The standard for the time being is to build to Baoji. The Railway Engineering Bureau will be reorganized into the Xi'an-Baoji Engineering Bureau, and while carrying out the Xi'an-Xianyang local and Wei River bridge projects, it will also begin surveying the Xianyang-Baoji route. (Special dispatch from the 18th)

Ping-Han Railway Reorganized into Twelve Sections 19

(Hankou) Recently, for the sake of quick handling and convenient command, the Ping-Han Railway has specially reorganized the entire line's traffic sections into three general sections and twelve sections (formerly three general sections and fifteen sections). The locations of the sectional stations are: 1. Changxindian, 2. Baoding, 3. Shijiazhuang, 4. Shunde, 5. Zhangde, 6. Xinxiang, 7. Zhengzhou, 8. Xuzhou, 9. Yancheng, 10. Xinyang, 11. Guangshui, 12. Dazhimen. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 18th)

President Wang to Visit Hangzhou 20

(Nanjing) President Wang is scheduled to go to Hangzhou on the 22nd to address the Zhejiang Provincial County Magistrate Training Class. After the event, he will take the opportunity to visit Hangzhou's construction and will stay for a day or two before returning to Nanjing. (Special dispatch from the 18th)

Hebei Provincial Government Stipulates Emergency Yellow River Projects; Plague Outbreak in Changyuan 21

(Tianjin) The Hebei Provincial Government has stipulated the following emergency Yellow River follow-up projects: (1) Embankment and reinforcement projects at Waicheji and Shitou Village; (2) Repair and reinforce the Hua Yang Dike; (3) Consolidate the dangerous works at Liuzhuang and Laodaba. The Construction Department has transferred all river soldiers and laborers to Guantai and has specially ordered the River Bureau to quickly recall them, concentrate their efforts, and carry out emergency works day and night to complete the emergency works before the flood season. (Special dispatch from the 18th)

(Tianjin) Zhang Qinglu, the magistrate of Changyuan County, went to the Taihang Dike on the 16th to inspect the retreat of water from the entire dike project and estimate the major repair plan. He also investigated the arable land mu in various villages. Ye Zhenmin, a member of the Civil Affairs Department, is supervising the repair of the city walls in Changyuan. (Special dispatch from the 18th)

(Kaifeng) The Provincial Government, considering that there are many remaining materials after the closure of the breach in Guantai, has telegraphed the Economic Committee to allocate them to Henan Province to facilitate flood prevention. (Special dispatch from the 18th)

(Tianjin) Changyuan has excessive humidity, and mosquitoes are breeding. A spring plague has been discovered. Two female teachers died of the epidemic in the girls' school on the 16th. Many people have died of the epidemic in the villages after the water receded. Zhang Qinglu, the magistrate of Changyuan County, sent Yang Shulin and Jiao Hongnian to the Yellow River Committee to request medicines. Zhang Yinglin, the magistrate of Puyang County, telegraphed the province that the Yellow River Conservancy Commission has measured the Jin Dike and decided to repair the section east of Qinghe to the Puyang County boundary, a length of 50 li. Thirteen kilometers have already been contracted, and construction is scheduled to begin on the 20th. The remaining sections are being contracted. The engineering office is located in three sections from Qinghe Tou Liutun to Hezhai. The county magistrate selects and recommends well-respected local gentry in the river area as the administrative staff for each section and two assistants to assist with the project. (Special dispatch from the 18th)

Jiangxi Province Prevents Floods 22

(Nanchang) In Jiangxi, from March 17th to April 18th, there has been continuous overcast and rainy weather, with only five sunny days in between. The rest has been overcast and rainy, often with sudden wind and rain, and lightning. Therefore, mountain floods have erupted, and rivers have risen sharply, with vast waters. In recent days, various counties have reported disasters, and agriculture has been greatly affected. Telecommunications and highway traffic between the provincial capital and various counties have been greatly disrupted. The provincial authorities are supervising their subordinates to do their best to prevent disasters. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 18th)

Han River Water Rises Sharply 23

(Hankou) The sky in Hubei is continuously rainy, and the Han River water has risen sharply, rising a total of 8.5 meters from the 9th to the 18th. The water levels in the upper reaches of Yu, Yi, and Sha have also increased. The river dikes are in a state of emergency. In addition, the wheat crops in various counties have been destroyed by accumulated rain, and the spring harvest is hopeless. Various counties in Huang and E are setting up altars to pray for clear weather. (Special dispatch from the 18th)

Cargo Ship Sinks Off the Coast of Haizhou; Twenty Crew Members Drown 24

(Changshu) The "Gongda" cargo ship from Hupu, carrying 200 tons, went to Haizhou to load bean cakes. It capsized in a windstorm in the Menshan area off the coast. The shipowner Jiang Datu and 19 crew members drowned. The loss is estimated at 40,000 gold. Four ships traveling with it were unharmed. (18th)

Xiang-Gan Bandit Special Commissioner Liu Yongchang Confirmed Killed; Wu Jietang Captured 25

(Hankou) In the middle of last month, the 18th Division encountered about 200 bandits of the Pseudo-5th Regiment while searching and suppressing scattered bandits in Foling Nanping and other places in Jiangxi. They immediately launched a head-on attack. At that time, a bandit with a pistol was commanding in front and was shot and killed by our troops. Later, documents such as the Sixth Sub-district Commander and Xiang-Gan Political Security Bureau Special Commissioner's warrant seals and stamps were found in the dry food bag on the bandit's back. Moreover, Zhu Bao and other captured bandits testified that the person killed was indeed the current Sixth Sub-district Commander and Xiang-Gan Political Security Bureau Special Commissioner, Liu Yongchang. Liu had previously served as the director of the Pseudo-Central Political Sub-bureau last year and was promoted to commander. He had fled with the Pseudo-5th Regiment to the Cha Zhi border, resulting in his death, etc. After repeated testimony by all the prisoners, it was confirmed to be true. It is now heard that the 行營方面 (Campaign Headquarters), based on the previous information from the Sui Jing Department stationed in Jiangxi, will award 500 yuan in accordance with the Bandit Suppression Reward Regulations to encourage them. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 18th)

Campaign Headquarters Inspects Henan-Hubei Troops 26

(Hankou) The Chairman's Campaign Headquarters, in order to examine the education, management, sanitation, internal affairs, weapons, horses, and mobilization preparation of the troops in Henan and Hubei provinces, and to seek improvement, has specially appointed inspectors to carry out inspections and has formed six inspection groups. Each group has one chief committee member and several inspection committee members. All expenses are paid by the Campaign Headquarters and should not be supplied by the troops. It is heard that the six groups of committee members have already set off in different directions and are carrying out their work simultaneously. The list of chief committee members is specially noted below: First Group - Yang Yuxun, Second Group - Zhang Duo, Third Group - Zhao Pu, Fourth Group - Lü Liepei, Fifth Group - Wu Dezhen, Sixth Group - Fu Wenyun. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 15th)

(Hankou) The Campaign Headquarters received a telegram on the 15th from Sun Yuanliang, the commander of the 88th Division, stating that the engineer battalion of this division captured Wu Jietang, the chairman of the Pseudo-Special Zone Revolutionary Committee and the pseudo-political commissar and cultural minister, near Changlong. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 18th)

(Taiyuan) Yan Xishan, having completed the mourning period for his late father, arrived in Bing from the riverbank at 11:00 a.m. on the 18th, with his scroll and counterfeit items. Key figures in the military and political circles and various agencies sent representatives to greet him outside the city. After Yan arrived at the Sui Jing Department, he immediately met with Zhao Pilian and other key figures to discuss public-owned enterprises, Datong-Pukou Railway work, and silver issues. The meeting lasted for about an hour before adjourning. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 18th)

(Taiyuan) A-Wang is inspecting various factories in the Northwest today and will meet with Yan in the evening to discuss various issues of the Mongolian Political Council. It has been decided that he will leave Bing the day after tomorrow. A-Wang has been urging Zhao Daiwen to take the position of deputy director of the Mongolian Guidance, but Zhao initially declined due to old age. He then agreed on how to take office, and I can assist in the process. (Special dispatch from the 18th)

Current Commentary

Further Explanation of the Mutual Aid and Self-Help Movement of National Goods Manufacturers 31

— Yan

Since the United States implemented its silver purchasing policy, artificially raising silver prices, the international currency war has become increasingly acute. China's silver reserves have been flowing out, creating an unprecedented massive surplus of silver exports. Although the government has implemented silver export taxes and balancing taxes to curb this trend, the sharp decline in silver reserves has caused social panic, credit contraction, and tight money. On the eve of the conclusion of the last National Assembly, the depth of the panic and the bleakness of the situation were rarely seen since the founding of the Republic. As a result, for several months, both the banking and money industries have uniformly tightened lending to preserve their strength and prepare for future difficulties. However, national goods industries and businesses, already suffering from the impact of the devaluation and dumping of foreign goods, now feel the pain of capital turnover and adjustment. The market has become stagnant, commodities have lost their circulation, and the unemployment problem has worsened. Such a recession is not a blessing for the future of national goods industries. National goods manufacturers and various national goods organizations in this city, aware of this situation, have initiated mutual aid and self-help movements, organizing groups such as the Joint Market, National Goods Alliance, and Citizens' National Goods Consumption Alliance. They are studying issues such as improving products, standardizing retail and wholesale prices, and developing foreign trade. Their efforts are commendable. However, in my opinion, the past promotion of national goods has not been perfect. I dare to offer my humble opinions.

China's national goods promotion movement has a long history. However, based on past experiences, it lacked an overall plan and a clear objective. The general opinion was that all national products should be promoted, and national goods manufacturers merely took advantage of the opportunity to promote their products. Once popular, they did not hesitate to cut corners to seek huge profits, disregarding the loss of credibility of national goods. Therefore, although the call for promoting national goods has been repeatedly raised, the results have been minimal. I believe that the national goods promotion movement is the only effective remedy for saving China. If used properly, it can bring the dead back to life. Otherwise, its effect will only be temporary excitement, merely creating opportunities for a small number of manufacturers. It should be understood that although China has been diligently promoting national goods in recent years, the import and sale of foreign goods have increased rather than decreased. Pessimists attribute this to the failure of the national goods movement. In fact, the types of foreign goods imported today are different from those in the past. Taking textiles as an example, in the early years of the Republic, the import of coarse cloth was the main category. In recent years, due to changes in social customs and the widespread sales of our own products, it has shifted from coarse cloth to fine cloth and wool textiles. From this perspective, if we loudly advocate for the promotion of domestically produced coarse cloth without seeking to save the massive imports of fine cloth and wool textiles, the lack of effectiveness can be easily predicted. Therefore, promoting national goods requires a thorough study of the import situation of foreign goods first, and then selecting the key ones, distinguishing between urgency, and promoting them one by one. For those that already have substitutes, technical improvements should be planned to reduce costs and assist in their promotion. As for those that currently have no substitutes, we should immediately take action, gather national talents, and divide the work to study imitation and stimulate investment interest. If we follow this approach, promoting several types each year, over time, not only will the results be considerable, but the foundation of national goods can also be expected to be consolidated. As the saying goes, "It takes a hundred years to cultivate a person." I believe that the completion of national goods promotion also requires this particularly long-term spirit, otherwise it will not succeed.

League of Nations Council Decides to Form a Thirteen-Nation Committee to Study Future Sanctions Measures; Germany Dissatisfied with League of Nations Resolution, Only Hopes for Remedial Steps 32

(Geneva) After the League of Nations Council passed the resolution proposed by France condemning Germany for violating the military clauses of the Treaty of Versailles, it immediately appointed representatives from Canada, Chile, Spain, France, Hungary, Italy, the Netherlands, Poland, Portugal, Turkey, the Soviet Union, and Yugoslavia to form a committee to consider plans to make the League of Nations Covenant more effective in the collective security organization and to ensure compliance with international instruments on which peace depends. Chu Nai announced the adjournment of the session. The next meeting is scheduled for May 20, and it is expected that the dispute between Italy and Abyssinia will be discussed at that time. British Foreign Secretary Simon has already left for Paris tonight and plans to fly back to London tomorrow morning. (17th Reuters Dispatch)

(Berlin) The German government has protested against the attitude taken by the United Kingdom at the Stresa Conference and the League of Nations Council. British Ambassador to Germany Phipps was invited to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs last night. Since Foreign Minister Neurath was not in Berlin, he was received by Deputy Foreign Minister Bülow, who lodged an oral protest in the name of the German government regarding the British attitude. According to reports, the British and Italian ambassadors to Germany sent copies of the Stresa Conference communiqué to the German government yesterday, regarding the reaffirmation of the obligations of the Locarno Treaty by the United Kingdom and Italy. At that time, the German government requested a clear explanation of this communiqué, especially whether the United Kingdom and Italy would treat Germany the same as they would treat France if they fulfilled the provisions of the Locarno Treaty if France invaded Germany. British Ambassador Phipps and Italian Ambassador Cerruti immediately replied in person in accordance with the spirit of the Stresa Conference communiqué. No communiqué regarding this meeting was issued by Berlin. (18th Havas Dispatch)

(Berlin) Since the League of Nations Council passed a resolution condemning Germany's rearmament, German newspapers have been unanimously indignant and protesting. German newspapers claim that the League of Nations has no legal basis for this move, and that the bridge between the League of Nations and Germany has been completely dismantled. The responsibility for rebuilding this bridge rests entirely with the League of Nations itself. As for Poland's attitude, Polish Foreign Minister Beck issued a declaration on Tuesday stating that Poland felt more stable today than ever before. However, when the League of Nations voted, Poland sided with the majority. It is unknown what changes in international relations occurred during this short period, but it is conceivable that it is related to Poland's unilateral declaration to abolish the minority treaties. Furthermore, according to German newspapers, the official declaration of the German government regarding the League of Nations' condemnation case will be decided after clarifying whether the voting countries have any auxiliary declarations. (17th National Dispatch)

(Berlin) Political circles commented on the League of Nations Council's unanimous passage yesterday of the resolution proposed by France condemning Germany's reintroduction of military service, stating that Germany could not recognize the Council as an organization with the authority to judge events in which it was involved. Therefore, Germany does not regard the Council's judgment as generally valid. The action in Geneva is seen as prolonging tensions in Europe and making Germany's return to the League of Nations even more distant. One political commentator said that France has severed the line of European negotiations, just as it forced Germany to withdraw from the League of Nations. Germans were deeply surprised by Simon's attitude at the Council yesterday, as he had frankly discussed everything with Hitler in Berlin. The Germans are not very angry with Poland, believing that Poland was forced to agree. The news of the Council's passage of the resolution has been telegraphed to Hitler, who is currently in southern Germany. Before Hitler returns to Berlin on the 19th for his birthday, Germany will not make any decision on how to deal with it, or the parliament should hold a national referendum to show Germany's unity. Political circles do not think so, saying that Germany's unity has already been proven. (18th Reuters Dispatch)

Outline of Franco-Soviet Agreement Decided by Foreign Ministers; To Unite and Strengthen the League of Nations 33

(Geneva) French Foreign Minister Laval and Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov held a meeting today to finalize the outline of the Franco-Soviet agreement. The wording of the agreement will be finalized after consulting with both governments. According to reports, the main points of the Franco-Soviet agreement stipulate that France and the Soviet Union will jointly request the League of Nations Council to submit a proposal to increase the effectiveness of Articles 10, 16, and 17 of the League of Nations Covenant. The principles of the agreement were discussed by Laval and Soviet Ambassador to France Potemkin a week ago, but some details remained unresolved. After the Laval-Litvinov meeting tonight, all difficulties have been eliminated. (17th Havas Dispatch)

(Paris) Reports state that French Foreign Minister Laval and Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov held an important meeting in Geneva yesterday afternoon, lasting four hours, to discuss the Franco-Soviet mutual assistance agreement, with legal experts from both countries participating. Laval returned to Paris today and will submit the draft agreement to the Cabinet meeting tomorrow for approval. It is also reported that the agreement will be initialed on Saturday. A telegram from the Geneva correspondent of the Morning Post confirms that Laval has successfully persuaded Litvinov to abandon the claim that the mutual assistance clause should take effect automatically. Therefore, if there is a need for assistance in the future, it should first be submitted to the League of Nations Council. The Council will convene a meeting within 24 hours if necessary, granting the countries concerned the freedom to act or reject it. (18th National Dispatch)

(Paris) The outline and details of the Franco-Soviet agreement have been agreed upon. The Morning Post reports that Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov originally intended for the mutual assistance system to be mechanically applied, but was persuaded by Foreign Minister Laval to abandon this idea. The Business Post reports that Poland is willing to continue its military alliance with France and amend the treaty to enable a completely mechanical application. Various newspapers commented on Turkey's request to abolish the military clauses of the Treaty of Lausanne. Le Journal stated, "Turkey's request to re-establish defensive works in the Dardanelles and Bosphorus straits is the most reasonable interpretation of the right to equal defense. Turkey has also clearly stated that free navigation will still be allowed after the straits are rearmed, which shows its goodwill." The Business Post stated, "Turkey's intention is that if the major powers can allow the Dardanelles Strait to be rearmed, the Balkan Entente countries can also agree to Bulgaria's rearmament, which is logical." (17th Havas Dispatch)

(Geneva) Czech Foreign Minister Beneš, Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu, Turkish Foreign Minister Rüştü, and French Foreign Ministry Secretary-General Léger all visited Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov. The Romanian Foreign Minister hosted a banquet for Litvinov, which was attended by representatives of the Little Entente. Later, Litvinov visited French Foreign Minister Laval. (17th TASS Dispatch)

(Moscow) During the extraordinary meeting of the League of Nations Council in Geneva to discuss the French protest and resolution, Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov said, "This issue may seem different in form for the relations between the member states of the League of Nations, but in reality, it definitely requires the attention of the League of Nations. Not only did the Soviet Union not participate in the Treaty of Versailles, but in general, it does not approve of this treaty, including Germany's disarmament. The Soviet Union's formal attitude towards this issue is as follows: We are members of the League of Nations and the Council. Now, someone is still formally a member of the League of Nations, but they have brazenly violated international treaties, which is no different from violating the League of Nations Covenant. As a result, their obligations to other member states have also been violated, creating a threat to peace. The League of Nations Covenant must first pay attention to whether a certain country is complying with its international obligations. Although I do not emphasize the form of this issue at first, I want to emphasize its reality. All countries have equal rights, and all countries have the undeniable right to protect themselves and take various measures to ensure this security. However, we recognize that the equality of armaments rights is based on an assumption, that is, this type of armament is only used as a means to defend its existing borders and security. But if the concrete facts have raised questions about this assumption, then what shall we do? In other words, if the purpose of armament is not to protect borders, but to invade borders, to use violent means to implement its revenge ideas, to destroy the security of neighboring countries and distant lands, to destroy world peace, and to let its tragic consequences descend upon the world, then what shall we do? At the same time, if there is a country whose leaders openly declare that their foreign policy is not only aimed at revenge, but also at the unlimited conquest of other people's territories and the destruction of the independence of various countries, and at the same time this policy is not only not revoked, but even constantly propagated to indoctrinate its people, if this is the case, then what shall we do when it demands or even realizes the right to rearm itself? If there is a country that has the above-mentioned plans, and its leaders are unwilling to guarantee that their plans will not be realized, unwilling to guarantee the safety of their neighbors near and far, unwilling to provide other countries with the guarantees that they are prepared to provide (including countries that are not suspected of having aggressive ambitions), then what shall we do? Can we turn a blind eye to these facts? We must obviously have a special attitude towards these facts."

Litvinov, in order to fully explain, compared international life to a city. Someone in a certain city privately hides weapons and publicly kills residents in neighboring streets or distant streets. Then, he asks the municipal authorities, saying that he is willing to protect a part of the area, so that it will not be trampled on, but the rest of the area is allowed to use force freely. Is the municipal authority willing to consider his "allowance"? "What we require of the League of Nations is to defend international life in all parts of the world, and we must not let go of the factors that create threats to peace."

Litvinov finally stated that if the country concerned can also attend and participate in the Council's current meeting, and can listen to its formal statement, abolish its policy of violent revenge and conquering others, and declare its willingness to participate in a collective organization to protect the security of all countries (including itself), then it will be overjoyed, "But this kind of hope cannot be realized after all, which is a pity. We must draw our conclusions, and what determines our attitude towards this resolution is these conclusions, and not just its formal motives. This attitude is by no means that the Treaty of Versailles and its various clauses that have already been broken are reasonable. This expresses the efforts of our Soviet government to create an international order to make it difficult to break peace. Only in this way can we conclude such treaties." (18th TASS Dispatch)

(Berlin) The German semi-official agency German Foreign Policy Commentary has responded to the anti-German remarks made by Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov at the League of Nations Council, stating that "Soviet Russia has nothing to seek in Geneva, and this has reached its extreme due to Litvinov's declaration. Litvinov's declaration, at first glance, does not seem to be for the purpose of being announced in Geneva, but for the recent US General Assembly. In any case, Litvinov's remarks are more suitable for the Soviet Union's People's Representative Assembly than for the League of Nations, because the League of Nations still claims to be the supreme judicial organ of civilized countries in the world. Litvinov's communist speech, its ability to incite hatred against national socialist Germany, can be compared with various conspiracies brewed by Moscow in other countries. Because Soviet Russia intends to systematically harm any country, and in order to prevent this kind of harm, countries around the world must organize large teams of secret detectives to declare war on Moscow's disturbers of the peace. Litvinov is not unaware of this, so he shamelessly occupies the position of commenting on others, and his shamelessness is astonishing. Litvinov's slanders and insults against Germany did not cause any protests on the part of the League of Nations, which can prove the spirit of the resolution. Indeed, when the League of Nations submitted the resolution for a vote, it had already determined its identity. As for Germany, people all over the country are questioning whether Geneva's actions will be beneficial to future continued negotiations." (18th National Dispatch)

MacDonald's Speech Urges Germans to Compromise; The Existence of the League of Nations Depends on Peacemakers; To Maintain Peace, Great Sacrifices Must Be Prepared 34

(London) British Prime Minister MacDonald gave a radio speech here tonight, describing the events of the Stresa Conference, and strongly urged the German people to contribute appropriately to the construction of mutual trust in coordination with other countries. MacDonald said that the German people should know how deeply their sympathetic friends felt pain when dealing with their worries recently. Britain did not bear any new responsibilities at the Stresa Conference. He dared to say that if the spirit of the Stresa Conference could be maintained and all its resolutions could be implemented, it would definitely be of great help in eliminating the haze and seeing the sun again. MacDonald then explained the difference between peace lovers and peacemakers, saying that the continued existence of the League of Nations and its success depend on peacemakers. Peacemakers must cater to the facts. He knew that loving peace and dreaming of peace were not enough. He deeply felt that for the sake of peace and for the sake of all great principles, he must be prepared to make sacrifices, and even great sacrifices, because he must deal with all the difficulties in the world. A large part of the world does not yet have an eager desire for peace. (17th Reuters Dispatch)

(London) Lower House opposition leader Lansbury requested Prime Minister MacDonald to report on the events in Stresa and Geneva. When answering, MacDonald expressed his approval of the League of Nations Council's resolution condemning Germany. MacDonald claimed that the League of Nations' action was a necessary measure after "Germany's attack on peace," and said that Germany's armament requirements and the way it announced these requirements greatly influenced the entire conversation, because "the reason we went to Stresa was to consider past policies and declarations in view of the decline in the status quo." MacDonald solemnly declared that Britain's only obligation was to be prepared to consult at any time when Austria's independence was in danger, and that Britain's policy was still based on the League of Nations Covenant. MacDonald concluded, "The representatives of the three countries participating in the Stresa Conference not only did not split due to various difficulties, but also united to find a peaceful solution to the current crisis." (17th National Dispatch)

Austrian Foreign Minister Meets with British, French, Italian, and Czech Foreign Ministers; Satisfactory Results of Discussions 35

Vienna - Foreign Minister Weidege met with British Foreign Secretary Simon, French Foreign Minister Laval, Italian Representative Aloisi, and Czech Foreign Minister Beneš in Geneva yesterday. Officials here solemnly stated that the Rome Conference will be convened on May 25. Weidege's meeting with representatives from Britain, France, Italy, and the Czech Republic was intended to inquire about their views on the Central European security system before the meeting, and no decisions were made. Weidege has just returned to China from Geneva, saying that the trip was very satisfactory. According to well-informed sources, not only can all the major powers understand all of Austria's needs, but some countries that have always taken a reserved attitude towards Austria's actions can now also understand all of Austria's needs. (18th Havas Dispatch)

Europe Caught in a Situation of Disputes Among Nations; Germany Will Formally Protest to the League of Nations 36

(Geneva) After the League of Nations resolved yesterday to condemn Germany's rearmament and violation of the Treaty of Versailles, it has now fallen into a maze of countless international disputes. The League of Nations now needs to consider the following points:

(1) The plan supported by Britain, France, and Italy allows Austria, Hungary, and Bulgaria to immediately double their armies and restore conscription.

(2) Yugoslavia and Romania, seeing that their neighbors have been allowed to lift treaty restrictions, will also demand increased armaments.

(3) The Soviet Union requires sanctions to be applied to the whole world, its purpose being in the Far East and Japan.

(4) Turkey may request to amend the Treaty of Neuilly, so that it can restore defense in the Tartar Strait.

(5) Reconciling the Italian-Abyssinian dispute. The resolution passed by the League of Nations stipulates that a special committee will be formed to formulate "several most effective methods to establish a security organization in accordance with the League of Nations Covenant, and especially to plan economic and financial sanctions methods, so that they can be implemented in the future against any country that directly betrays treaties and endangers peace." The League of Nations' passage of this resolution this time is generally regarded as a great victory for France over Germany. Poland's participation in the vote is truly surprising. It is still remembered that a few days ago, Polish Army Minister Pilsudski declared that Poland was unwilling to sign any treaty that would harm its feelings with Russia and Germany. However, Pilsudski's remarks were informal expressions during his conversation with British Lord Privy Seal Eden. It is learned here that the Berlin newspapers are attacking the League of Nations resolution fiercely, and express that this act is nothing more than the League of Nations' consistent policy of discriminating against Germany. It is said that President Hitler and his advisors are preparing to submit a formal protest to the League of Nations Council next week. (18th National Dispatch)

Verdict in French Espionage Case: Russian Mastermind Sentenced to Five Years 37

(Paris) The most sensational espionage case in France since the Great War concluded its trial today. Twenty-one individuals, including two American spouses named Switz, were found guilty of leaking military secrets. However, the Switz couple have been released due to the relatively minor nature of their offenses. A Russian national named Stahl, 48, believed to be a Russian spy, was sentenced to five years in prison. Several others received sentences ranging from one to five years. (Reuters, 17th)

(Paris) Stahl and his thirty accomplices, accused of supplying military secrets to Soviet Russia, have been sentenced. Stahl received a five-year prison sentence, a fine of three thousand francs, and a five-year ban from residing in France. Former Colonel Mauling and Romanian Berkovec also received similar sentences, as they had been receiving monthly payments of four thousand francs for leaking blueprints of tanks and military telephone equipment. Stahl vehemently denied his guilt, claiming he only assisted a teacher named Mehmet in purchasing photographic equipment, resulting in a three-year sentence. An American couple named Switz received ninety-five thousand francs, but they were spared punishment due to a "Royal Certificate." Eleven individuals remain at large, including a translator for Naval Captain Martin. The remaining nine were sentenced to prison terms ranging from ten months to four years. (National Telegram, 18th)

(Paris) France is continuing to strengthen its eastern defenses. The 8th Infantry Regiment, formerly stationed in southern France, has been transferred to Belfort to garrison two fortresses. Furthermore, the 3rd Battalion of the 28th Regiment and the 1st Battalion of the 15th Regiment have also been deployed to Longuyon. (National Telegram, 18th)

Little Entente Joins South American Non-Aggression Pact: Romanian Foreign Minister Signs on Behalf 42

(Geneva) The Little Entente nations have recently joined the South American Non-Aggression Pact initiated by Argentinian Foreign Minister Saavedra. According to the pact's provisions, American nations and League of Nations member states mutually agree not to engage in aggression. It was signed by a majority of American nations in the capital of Argentina on October 10, 1933. Italy and Spain subsequently joined the agreement. During the current League of Nations Council meeting, both the Argentinian representative to the League of Nations, Gastillo, and the Chairman of the Permanent Political Council of the Little Entente, Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu, were in Geneva. Titulescu signed the agreement on behalf of the Little Entente nations. (Havas, 18th)

Hong Kong Economic Committee Issues Economic Survey Report 46

(Hong Kong) The Hong Kong Economic Committee, after an eight-month investigation, released its report today, advocating that the Hong Kong government's economic policies should avoid drastic changes. The report acknowledges that Chinese tariffs have significantly impacted Hong Kong trade and proposes that Hong Kong merchants establish manufacturing zones within the Chinese tariff zone on Hong Kong land. It also advocates for closer economic cooperation with China, particularly Guangzhou. The committee opposes enacting tariffs for negotiation purposes but states that Hong Kong should seek free or preferential trade with China in return for protecting Chinese customs duties. (Reuters, 18th)

Indian Council of State Adjourns Sine Die; Passes Motion of Loyalty to the British Crown 47

New Delhi: After unanimously passing a motion of loyalty to the British Crown, the Council of State adjourned sine die today. (Reuters, 17th)

British Archaeologist Receives Gold Medal 48

(London) The distinguished archaeologist Sir Stein received the Gold Medal from the Archaeological Society today, in recognition of his outstanding contributions to the field of archaeology. Sir Stein was born in Hungary 72 years ago and has led archaeological expeditions to various parts of the world. From 1888 to 1899, he collected antiquities in Kashmir and along the Afghan border. In 1900, he led a team for the Indian government to search for artifacts in Chinese Turkestan. From 1906 to 1908, he engaged in archaeological and geographical exploration in Central Asia and western China. Last year, the Royal Anthropological Institute awarded him the Huxley Medal. (Reuters, 17th)

Great Achievement in Conquering the Pacific: American Large Aircraft Safely Arrives in Honolulu; Completes the First Leg of the Sino-American Flight; Sets New Record with Average Speed of 120 mph 49

Honolulu: The American Flying Boat No. 5, weighing 30 tons, arrived here today from Alameda, completing the first leg of its journey from San Francisco across the Pacific to China. All previous records for this route have been broken, covering 2,100 miles in 18 hours, with an average speed of over 120 mph. In addition to the six crew members, the plane also carried 10,000 pieces of mail. (Reuters, 17th)

Honolulu: The "Oriental Flying Boat", a 19-ton aircraft pioneering the airmail route between California, USA, and China, departed from Alameda, California, and arrived here at 7:59 AM this morning, one minute ahead of schedule. This event marks a major achievement in humanity's conquest of the Pacific. As the plane landed safely this morning, welcomers waved flags and cheered, accompanied by military music. A squadron of US Army aircraft and various other aircraft circled overhead, welcoming the "Oriental Flying Boat" upon its arrival. The aircraft departed yesterday evening, guided by signals from the Honolulu radio station. Following the landing, senior US government officials sent congratulatory telegrams. Postmaster General Farley and Democratic Senator McAdoo praised the success of the flight. It is said that this flight did not involve significant danger, as advancements in aviation have progressed far beyond the times when earlier aviators sacrificed their lives. Whether the aircraft will fly to Guangzhou, China, to complete the proposed airmail route remains unknown. In addition to the pilot, Captain Mojeck, the crew includes a co-pilot and five engineers. (National Telegram, 17th)

American Textile Industry Uneasy Over Japanese Dumping; Roosevelt Orders Tariff Commission Investigation 51

(Washington) The American textile industry is uneasy due to the impact of Japanese cotton textile imports into the United States. Several textile mills in New England have already ceased operations. President Roosevelt has ordered an immediate investigation into the potential dangers of Japanese bleached cotton textile imports to the American textile industry. (Havas, 17th)

(Tokyo) According to the Tokyo Newspaper, American cotton textile industry associations in various regions have repeatedly petitioned the State Department, requesting that the government raise import tariffs on Japanese cotton textiles. President Roosevelt yesterday ordered the Tariff Commission to investigate the import volume of Japanese cotton textiles and their relationship to domestic products. The investigation results of the commission have a close relationship to the future market of Japanese cotton textiles, so it is worthy of attention from the Japanese government. Furthermore, according to Undersecretary of State Philipps, if a particular industrial sector in one country is threatened by the same goods from another country, it is often necessary to implement high tariffs, and reciprocity is not feasible. (United China News, 18th)

Fishing Conditions in Twelve Counties of Shandong 86

(Jinan) Zhao Yunxie, a member of the Provincial Government, investigated the fishing industry in twelve counties, including Weixian, Changyi, Yexian, Zhaoyuan, Huangxian, Penglai, Fushan, Wendeng, Pingdu, Jimo, Haiyang, and Rongcheng. Upon returning to Jinan, he stated that there are 24,477 fishing households, 15,122 fishing boats, and an annual fish production of 104,962,719,700 jin, valued at over 500 million. In recent years, production has been nearly halved due to the impact of Japanese fishing boats and insufficient fish salt supply. In the past, sales extended as far as Hong Kong and the Northeast. However, due to customs restrictions, ships under twenty tons are not allowed to export, resulting in a significant reduction. The annual demand for fish salt is over one million dan, but the Salt Transport Office only allows the release of 420,000 dan, which is insufficient for use. This is a major reason for the decline of the fishing industry. The Provincial Government has decided to comprehensively coordinate relief measures. (Special Dispatch, 18th)
