Free Talk

Miscellaneous Discussions on Humor 252

— Meng Jia

The prevalence of "humor movements" can be described as "unparalleled" in the history of Chinese cultural movements. However, if we puncture this paper tiger, we find nothing inside. Some use false humor to feign superiority, making trivial and harmless satirical remarks to gain applause; others use humor to express their feelings and sentiments, like "hiding bitterness in bitter tea," sitting on a sofa, smoking a cigarette, sipping fragrant tea, smacking their lips, sighing with an air of "leisure," then opening a 20th-century joke book, saying a few "relaxed," half-witty and half-serious words, eliciting "knowing smiles" from everyone. Thus, "humor," "humor," eventually even the clown's antics on stage are brought in to add to the collection.

However, it would be a great mistake to say that the humor movement is merely a tool for ambitious people to climb the ladder, "irrelevant to the fate of the nation." The reason why the humor movement became so popular is not solely due to the promoters, but also has its objective social basis. Many people are dissatisfied with reality, so they use "jesting without malice" to satirize the objects they hate, which becomes the only way to vent their anger and resentment. From this, we can say that the emergence of the humor movement is not accidental, but has its rational reasons for existence. Thorough and fierce laughter is necessary, and a gentle, non-satirical sneer is also needed. "Humor is a wonderfully effective corrector. Therefore, humorous comedy is a gentle satirical comedy that points out shortcomings and teaches how to remove them—it is a mirror placed before people, not a mirror that makes them panic and want to find ropes or nails upon seeing it, but a mirror that makes them feel the need to wash their face and shave."

The function and power of humor are evident here. It is true that humor is "not thorough enough to expose reality." However, it is not necessarily the case that "it often turns the public's determination to fight into a wisp of smoke" or "turns the butcher's ferocity into a lighthearted smile." If that is really the case, it is the fault of "humor," not the fault of the humor movement. The problem lies in how to remove those glib, witty, and slapstick elements, "knowing smiles," "expected reversals," etc., from humor, and transform it into a tool to educate the general public, make them aware of the ugliness of reality, and make them feel the need to tell it (reality) to wash its face and shave. Although humor is "not thorough enough to expose reality," it can still expose reality (though not "thoroughly"). By satirically exposing certain aspects of the dark side of reality, even if it cannot "comprehensively" expose it and give us a way out, it has fulfilled its task and function by helping the general public recognize the aspects of reality and making them feel the need to reform it.

Accepting Criticism and Scolding 253

— Hu Yifan

In a recent issue of "Free Talk," Mr. Tang Tao published an article entitled "Accepting Criticism," in which he discussed the issue of accepting criticism and scolding. I think this is worth paying attention to.

In the section where Mr. Tang Tao addressed this issue, he said:

"But now it is said that even truth is crying in pain, because critics have scolded everything to the ground.

"In fact, there are different kinds of scolding. Careless scolding that starts with 'damn it' is certainly unacceptable; but scathing scolding that can pinpoint the flaws and enumerate them in detail can still be accepted."

I don't know if the "now it is said that even truth is crying in pain" referred to here is really "because critics have scolded everything to the ground." I don't want to delve into it too deeply, because Mr. Tang's article has already answered it. And Mr. Tang Tao's opinion is the opposite. So when he talked about scolding, he conceded again and again and said, "In fact, there are different kinds of scolding." Then he pointed out that there are "unacceptable" "careless scolding" and "scathing scolding that can pinpoint the flaws and enumerate them in detail" in criticism, which "can still be accepted."

He feels that the alleged truth is crying in pain, which is really impossible to completely write off the critics, because he believes that critics "are also human beings" and "they understand other people's works."

I agree with Mr. Tang Tao's statement, but I still want to add some opinions.

In fact, to talk about the issue of accepting criticism is a matter of contending for truth. The attitude of critics needs to be serious and objective, and they cannot simply resort to careless scolding or dogmatism, so as to arouse the antipathy of the criticized—the writers, or even "ignore it." This seems to be unnecessary to say a second time, everyone understands. But even if you do this, as Mr. Tang Tao said, can "scathing scolding that can pinpoint the flaws and enumerate them in detail" really "still be able to" ask people—those criticized writers—to humbly "accept" it?

Nothing is clearer than what Mr. Tang Tao himself said! Because those writers had already "ignored it all together, and, 'as usual, there are always a few words to say. Or they say: "This is a Taiwanese!" Or they say: "This is a certain faction!" And the more thorough one is: "Hey! You're pointing at your own nose!" They are "denouncing criticism" and "resisting criticism!"'"

No matter how well-intentioned and objective a critic you are, what can you do with these people?

Here, we have to come into contact with the writer's subjective understanding and the writer's own artistic cultivation. If we really want to talk about criticism and accepting criticism.

For a writer who has long been despaired of, or, in other words, whose understanding has completely turned backwards, even if there is criticism that "can still be accepted"—"scathing scolding that can pinpoint the flaws and enumerate them in detail"—the critic is completely useless to him; because he has already said to you: "Hey! You are Taiwanese! You are a certain faction! You are pointing at your own nose." Can you still talk to him about accepting criticism? No matter how different your scolding is, before your civilized scathing scolding even begins, he has already "ignored it all together," or even become embarrassed and angry, "spitting blood on people." This has become his consistent attitude. At this time, can you have a better way to accommodate him than to ruthlessly expose his true colors in the open air, so that he can humbly accept criticism again?

Well-intentioned criticism with theoretical basis can have a critical effect on a criticized—a writer—only if the person's understanding is vague, or his worldview is certain but his artistic cultivation is not enough. It is possible to expect such a person to humbly accept criticism. If a critic can grasp their weaknesses, then at this time, you can bluntly say to him: "You can't be so lazy and opportunistic!" Or say: "This is not the way, you've gotten into a dead end!" Or even say: "You're doing the enemy's work!" No matter how you enumerate and scold, he will not refuse you, as long as the critic's own attitude is sincere and serious. And this scathing scolding is no longer scolding, but has become guidance, correction, and encouragement. A writer who has his own correct worldview or is willing to improve, will not only "still be able to accept" such scathing scolding criticism, but will definitely be willing to accept it from the bottom of his heart.

But at the same time, don't forget the critic himself: what Mushanokoji Saneatsu said: Critics "are also human beings," is true: saying that they "will not fundamentally understand other people's works" is a big mistake. But it is not necessarily true to believe that every critic can "understand other people's works." Why? Because among critics, there are critics who only know how to scold carelessly, and there are even critics who are full of poisonous sores. Can you pay attention to such critics' arbitrary scolding and biting, and nonsense? In this situation, the enlightened writer's response to this "absolutely absurd critic" is no longer "accepting criticism," but must be a head-on blow (!). Therefore, there needs to be a sound "critic" of critics who stubbornly seek the truth.

Therefore, my opinion is: when it comes to criticism and "accepting criticism," in fact, there are different kinds of scolding. Careless scolding is certainly unacceptable; but in theory, "scathing scolding that can pinpoint the flaws and enumerate them in detail" may "still be able to be accepted," but in fact, it still depends on what kind of critic it is, and what kind of) writer is being criticized.

Yellow Fur Peak 254

— Zhou Qi

The name of the mountain peak is "Yellow Fur Peak."

How many feet above sea level is Yellow Fur Peak? No surveying team has ever been there, so it's not very clear. However, according to the reprinted Japanese military maps, it is drawn with dense black lines in layers. We climbed this Yellow Fur Peak, looking up for three whole days.

On the third day, we climbed to the top of Yellow Fur Peak, and saw that the surrounding mountains had all lowered their heads. Higher than this mountain peak was only our "Old Heaven." However, sometimes Old Heaven also lowered its head, scattering clouds and mist, and kissing the mountain peak, or putting a hat on the mountain peak.

When we arrived at Yellow Fur Peak, we quickly set up our tents and prepared to live there for three days. If we didn't see any signs of bandits within three days, then we would consider our information inaccurate and move on to the next mountain. In any case, in these two weeks, we had to search in the mountains, because the order specified that this group of people should be searched for in the mountains.

It was spring, and green grass was growing on the mountain peak. The sun was very warm, and the brothers wearing cotton military uniforms were sweating profusely. Because they couldn't sweat comfortably, some of them pulled out the cotton padding from their military uniforms to use as toilet paper, using the cotton as toilet paper. The coolies, seeing that they hadn't been carrying loads for several days in a row, looked at the sky and thought of home in their spare time. The radio's charging machine was "clapping" on the hillside. There were many radio waves in the sky, and the person with the earphones clipped to his ears was looking for his own signal in the radio waves. Sometimes, they even heard a song from Shanghai or Little Luzon… The days passed peacefully for two days.

But an unexpected thing happened on the evening of the second day. Because everyone was already sleeping in their tents, only the sentries knew about it at first.

It was a sky with a big moon, but after midnight, clouds began to gather. The clouds became denser and thicker, and finally obscured the moon. From the corner of the sky, a storm came sweeping in. In a few minutes, the storm was raging wildly. Finally, it blew the raindrops down from the clouds. At first, it was small, but it became bigger and bigger. At this time, a roar arose in the mountains. "Whump—whump—," like countless people rushing, shouting. "Snap," the radio's antenna pole broke, "whump," the tent was blown away, followed by the miserable cries of a group of people drenched in the rain. The coolies, covered with a few stalks of straw, ran wildly in the dark mountains in a panic. The commanding officer, flustered, got up to check the sentries. The wind was blowing harder and harder. The rain was falling harder and harder. The climate changed drastically into winter. The raindrops immediately turned into freezing rain. Before long, the sentries fell, the coolies fell, the mules and horses fell, and clothes and boxes were washed down the mountain by the mountain torrents… The wind and rain became even greater. At this time, Yellow Fur Peak was a scene of turmoil and misery.

The next morning, suddenly, the wind and rain stopped. Someone clever, in the middle of the night, had paved the ground with thick glass. The branches, the green grass, the coolies' faces, the gun barrels, were all inlaid with glass. The beards, the long hair, the mules' and horses' tails, the tassels tied to the ends of the guns, were all hung with glass wind chimes. The tents that hadn't been blown away were frozen solid, and the eyebrows and hair of the living people had all turned white. The bugler blew the assembly call, but they had to assemble and go down the mountain, but the bugler couldn't blow the bugle. The bugle was completely filled with ice… The top of the mountain was still a scene of turmoil and misery.

"Go down the mountain, go down the mountain, if we don't go down the mountain, we'll die."

The group could no longer resist the cold. Coerced by the power of nature, they could only go down the mountain. But all the things were frozen solid and could no longer be taken away. Some people slipped on the slope and were smashed to pieces on the steep cliffs below.

When going down the mountain, it was still a scene of turmoil and misery.

After walking down the slope for more than a dozen miles, as if by magic, the red sun reappeared, shining on our soaked clothes, and the sky was clear. We knew that Old Heaven was playing a joke on us. But when we looked back at the mountain peak, the mountain peak was in the clouds and mist, and we really couldn't tell whether we were awake or dreaming.

But what about the people left on the mountain peak? They sacrificed themselves before they even encountered the enemy.

Notes on Examining the Exhibits of the Chinese Art International Exhibition (3) 255

— Cao Juren

Rooms four and five display porcelain from the Song and Ming dynasties onward, totaling 314 pieces. In this era of decline of Chinese porcelain, looking at the exquisite products of the Northern Song Dynasty's Ding Kiln, Jun Kiln, Ru Kiln, Official Kiln, Longquan Kiln, Ge Kiln, Jianyang Kiln, and various other kilns, and then looking at the progress in color and style of the Southern Song Dynasty, Jizhou Kiln, Ming Yongle Kiln, and Xuande Kiln, one cannot help but sigh at the aging of the nation, which is already evident in the production of these daily necessities. Jingdezhen Kiln, since ancient times, has combined the advantages of various kilns, and the utensils made are all-encompassing, but now everything is not as good as before. Perhaps the glory of Chinese porcelain will end together with Jingdezhen! There are many people at the exhibition who, after seeing the , from the early Qing Dynasty, Kangxi, Yongzheng, and Qianlong reigns, not only are the bright reds moving, but the sky blues, yellows, and blown purples are even more vivid, and they praised them one after another. But their everyday household eating utensils are either Japanese or Western, and they have almost forgotten the products of Jingdezhen!

Room six displays ancient books, jade artifacts, cloisonné enamel, carved lacquer, and selected examples of archaeological items, etc. The ancient books section has not yet arrived completely. There are carved editions from the Southern Song, Jin, Yuan, and Qing dynasties, mainly carved editions. I have already praised the compiler's insight in my previous article. The Sino-Barbarian Dictionary, an official carved edition from the Hongwu reign, is carved with extreme precision. In addition to the carved editions, there are two manuscript copies of the Legend of the Moon-Worshipping Pavilion and the Legend of the Spiritual Treasure Sword, which are truly exquisite and lovely. Living in this circle of crude and shoddy Shanghai-style crafts, seeing these fine products of the handicraft era, one cannot help but sigh that people of ancient and modern times are incomparable. I have never had any particular fondness for jade artifacts. Apart from the value of the objects themselves, they have no significant meaning in cultural history. Many ladies are very enthusiastic about them, wishing they could break the glass and compare the jade artifacts in the cabinet with the jade bracelets on their arms. Several jade artifacts from the Qianlong reign are carved with extreme precision, which further attracts the ladies' affections. The archaeological items group, such as stone axes, stone knives, bone arrowheads, bone hairpins, bronze ge, bronze spears, etc., many have already been seen in the Anyang excavation reports and in books such as The Dawn of Eastern Culture. Seeing the actual objects naturally makes one feel more interested. As far as I know, the achievements of the Academia Sinica in excavating in Henan and the scope of their research are much broader than this. We hope that in the future, Henan will become the Pompeii of the East.

Of course, I should declare my own position: I am looking at that exhibition with the significance of studying ancient Chinese culture. Perhaps many words have offended the dignity of artists and antique collectors. Forgive me! Forgive me! (The End)

Mr. Juqing (17) 256

— Ke Ling

Then the test question was brought up. What Mr. Juqing wanted to ask Principal Zhang was the meaning of the four characters "stubborn and ignorant."

Principal Zhang did not answer the test question. His face changed color in waves, and every vein stood out on his temples. He slammed the table and cursed loudly, and finally got into a twisted brawl with Mr. Juqing. Mr. Juqing was pushed and shoved to the street, and then twisted towards the Public Security Bureau.

The quiet small street was rippled with excitement, and there were as many people watching the fun as there were watching a race.

Principal Zhang and Mr. Juqing were twisting and wrestling in the front, surrounded by the lanky man and the teacher with the neck hair; Mr. Juqing's dozen or so students followed behind, and there were also many men and women onlookers, like a group of tadpoles in a spring pond, crowding and squeezing in the street.

"Look, Principal Zhang wrote the wrong character!"

All the way, Mr. Shi Qing shouted loudly with a hoarse voice:

"Principal Zhang wrote the wrong character, what a disgrace!"

But after arriving at the Public Security Bureau, Mr. Juqing didn't even have a chance to say a few words. They didn't even need to ask who was right and who was wrong. They just let Principal Zhang passionately explain everything to the patrol captain, and Mr. Juqing was arrested.

Mrs. Juqing, in a frenzy, ran crying and sobbing through the streets, and almost ran through the homes of several gentlemen in the town.

She kowtowed to everyone she met, with tears and snot, begging them to rescue her husband. She had experienced so many tragic encounters in her life, but had never run into such a disaster; terror and anxiety dominated her central nervous system, and she became like someone who had completely lost consciousness.

It wasn't until after dusk that she got a business card from Chu Runfu, the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce. When Mr. Juqing came out of the detention center of the Public Security Bureau, it was already 11 o'clock at night, and everyone in the town was asleep.

After returning home, Mr. Juqing didn't say a word from beginning to end. His eyes were even more deeply sunken in, emitting a shimmering light; his face was as expressionless as if it were cast in iron. When asked if he wanted to drink tea, he didn't say a word; when told to rest, he didn't say a word. All were silent.

Suddenly, in the silence, he roared fiercely, his voice shrill and high-pitched:

"What law did I break to be detained!"

He punched the table, and the Mei Foo oil lamp suddenly jumped up, and the light dimmed and flickered as if it were about to go out. Mrs. Juqing and her daughter-in-law were horrified beside her, shivering in waves.

"I don't want this old life anymore, I'll fight you!"

Bang! Another punch. He stood up to rush out, but was pulled back by his mother and daughter-in-law, and pressed back into the chair.

He sat down weakly, feeling an overwhelming fatigue all over his body.

What would happen next? This study, this lonely, gray home? This insult that swept away all dignity?…

In a daze, he saw hundreds of snobbish eyes shooting at him like random arrows, and hundreds of mocking faces demonstrating against him. Thousands and hundreds of golden stars were dancing wildly before his eyes, and a huge dark cloud was quickly pressing down on his forehead.

His body suddenly fell from the chair to the ground, and he knew nothing. (The End)

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Random Talks

Students Attend National Goods Pledge Ceremony 257

— Feng

This year is the student national goods year, and yesterday was the day for students to take an oath to use national goods. From now on, students will bear the two major missions of using national goods themselves and persuading relatives and friends to use national goods. This kind of responsibility is inherently unshoulderable and obligatory.

But to persuade others to use national goods, one must first use national goods oneself. This goes without saying, otherwise one cannot even open one's mouth. The student national goods year does not mean that students should use national goods, but non-students do not necessarily have to use national goods, nor does it mean that students should use national goods, but should not use national goods as soon as they leave school. This meaning should be understood by everyone. In my opinion, students, especially university students, should use national goods even more, because the common problem of university students is that as soon as they become university students, they become arrogant and speak of foreign things, speak of foreign things all the time - not to mention those who have studied abroad - they regard national goods as worthless weeds. If they are not wearing Western suits and leather shoes, they seem to lose the dignity and personality of a university student. A kind of contempt for national goods is naturally deeply planted in their hearts. Therefore, middle school students admire the airs of university students and often wear Western suits and leather shoes, and all their products are imported goods. The formation of this kind of psychology, fundamentally speaking, is more than enough to destroy the country and exterminate the species.

Because university students are the role models for middle school students, and middle school students are the role models for elementary school students, if university students can develop the habit of using national goods, then the habits of middle and elementary school students will also be easily developed. As for using national goods, it is originally the national duty of every citizen. Whether our country's national and social economy has reached the end of its rope, we should not fail to use national goods, even if the national and social economy is relatively abundant, we should also use national goods, because abandoning national goods and using foreign goods will inevitably result in a day when we reach the end of our rope.

Today, I want to say that not only students, but I also urge the rich to use national goods, which is even more important than those who are relatively poor, because wealthy families spend thousands of taels on a car, and dozens of yuan on a sofa, while poor families, even if they want to use non-national goods, do not have the purchasing power. Therefore, it is more important for the rich to use national goods than for the poor. I also urge businessmen to use national goods, and non-businessmen should pay even more attention to using national goods, because ordinary people have an extremely weak ability to distinguish between national goods and non-national goods, and there are generally unscrupulous merchants who only seek profit and often pass off non-national goods as national goods, mixing fish eyes with pearls everywhere. Such merchants should also wake up early and thoroughly reform themselves. Not only will they avoid the warnings of bystanders, but they will also be condemned by their own conscience, which they may never forget.

Tonghui Silk Shop 258

— Si Quan

When the first fish vendor passed through the central market, four or five craftsmen from Tonghui Silk Shop were on high ladders, decorating a grand sale archway with colorful green cloth. Manager Mr. Zhou, like a monkey, jumped from the shop to the street and back, helping to organize the fabrics. Tiny beads of sweat dotted his forehead, and his wrinkled yellow face shone as if it were a newly sculpted Buddha statue, every cell radiating with hope. This was the first time the fish

Page 18

vendor's second brother had seen Mr. Zhou so energized since the beginning of spring.

Tonghui Silk Shop is the oldest brand name in the whole county. Everyone clearly remembers the gilded characters on the two plaques hanging on either side of the entrance. The shop was founded in the twelfth year of the Guangxu Emperor's reign, specializing in purchasing various provincial silks and satins. However, the gilt is now peeling, and the underlying mud is exposed on the wooden boards. Yet, Manager Mr. Zhou takes pride in this, believing that a brand-name shop should have such ancient gilded plaques!

Mr. Zhou started as an apprentice and only rose to the position of manager after the first revolution. He has seen and learned much, and his primary creed is that business should be conducted with harmony to generate wealth. Apprentices must not deviate from the rules, and he himself was favored by the shop owner and promoted to his current position because of this. Every day after closing, during dinner, he would drink wine and recount his history of over a decade with the shop to the apprentices. He could remember the exact year and month of every event: the year he joined the shop, the year he was officially promoted to shop clerk, the year a certain apprentice was dismissed for being slow to serve a customer. He would solemnly recount these stories in detail every day, never mixing up the order or accidentally omitting anything. Therefore, since he took over, he has monopolized the business of all the wealthy families in the county. He frequented the homes of local gentry and dignitaries, appearing to be a very important person. When a family was marrying off a daughter or taking a bride, he would immediately bring the latest styles of goods to their door for them to choose from, and his prices were fairer than those of his competitors. Tonghui Silk Shop's reputation grew year by year, while the characters on the two plaques of the brand-name shop became almost unrecognizable.

Many silk and satin shops opened in the eastern and western markets, but none could surpass Tonghui. In terms of goods, service, and prices, no one could match Mr. Zhou's business acumen. When people spoke of the silk and satin industry in the county, they only mentioned our Mr. Zhou's Tonghui Silk Shop.

Mr. Zhou is now over fifty years old. One could say that he has lived his life for Tonghui Silk Shop. He gets up early and goes to bed late, just like when he was an apprentice, except for the few glasses of old wine he drinks at dinner. However...

The ghost-like county bus station suddenly opened long-distance bus routes. The road, built with funds raised from various shops, brought an irreparable and fatal blow. The sudden change in fashion throughout the county was a strange phenomenon. Western-style clothing often flashed before Mr. Zhou's eyes in front of Tonghui Silk Shop, and women's dresses were especially eye-catching, like colorful butterflies. Tonghui Silk Shop, which prided itself on being a brand-name store, suddenly saw its latest silk and satin colors dim in comparison. It barely made any sales each day, while expenses increased in reverse proportion. This long-distance bus route brought a continuous stream of taxes and levies with names that were difficult to pronounce. Seeing this ominous phenomenon, Mr. Zhou resigned from his position to the shop owner almost daily.

Bao Kang and Xiang Tai in the eastern and western markets have successively closed down. Several silk and satin businesses, struggling to take their last breath, had to imitate the Western-style sales of the other end of the long-distance bus route, erecting colorful archways and holding grand sales with the sound of Western drums pounding all day long. When Mr. Zhou learned of this, he shook his head and sighed even more. No business was coming in, and now they had to add these extravagant expenses. "It's truly self-inflicted!" he exclaimed when the apprentices told him that a certain shop was holding a grand sale. But the second piece of news arrived: Sheng Fuzhuang and Qian Dahao were crowded with people, and they could make half a thousand in sales each day. Mr. Zhou was astonished by this contradictory situation and realized the method of raising prices. He was tormented by the words "unorthodox," so he stopped drinking wine at dinner and quickly ate his meal to discuss with the shop owner whether this method could be implemented.

Finally, on this morning, a colorful archway was erected in front of Tonghui Silk Shop. This was Mr. Zhou's final decision. "If business doesn't improve," he said, "I'm quitting. I haven't seen such a market in decades!"

Memories of Rain 259

— Li Ni

Waking up early and pushing open the south-facing glass window, I felt a little unhappy. The plum rain was still falling, drizzling like silk threads, weaving into a crystal-like curtain hanging in front of the window.

The sky was piled with gray clouds, layer upon layer, densely frozen, making the sky gloomy and low, as if it were collapsing on people's heads. In the distance, a patch of jungle newly dressed in tender green clothes was obscured by the misty rain, like a thin veil. The winding path of the field ridge from the village entrance to the county town was already muddy, and several villagers silently held up their rain gear and walked along laboriously. The dirty water and soybean-milk-like mud in the small puddles splashed all over their clothes.

"Annoying plum rain season, it's truly suffocating!" I sighed deeply, murmuring in my heart.

Rain, in itself, is very closely related to me. But I like the surging, torrential rain and the gurgling, pouring incessant rain, and I don't like this drizzling, silky, hair-like plum rain of Jiangnan. However, this stampeding torrential rain is something I can enjoy contentedly very few times each year in Jiangnan. When the plum rain falls every year, it always confines me to a narrow room that is too small to turn around in, silently worrying, facing the morbid rain outside the window, and reminiscing about the unrestrained, surging rain of the South—Siam.

At that time, I was staying in the South, and it was then that I deeply understood the elegant taste of rain and formed an extremely fond connection with rain.

In the hot tropics of the South, there is also a rainy season every year, lasting for a long one or two months, just like the plum rain season in Jiangnan. But it is not like the plum rain in Jiangnan, which flutters silkily all day long, making people's emotions feel overly sad and melancholic! When the rain has not yet fallen, the sky is as blue as the blue sea, and the sun fiercely emits heat, scorching people's heads and backs with all its might. No one would believe that this beautiful, clear sky would bring a torrential rain in two or three quarters of an hour! However, at this very moment, this clear, beautiful blue sky changes color. Black clouds stretch out from the corners of the horizon and quickly fill the entire sky. The sun also retracts its heat and escapes into the gaps in the clouds. The wind blows madly, getting stronger and stronger, shaking the lush green trees in the fields, making them roar like a tiger, creating the atmosphere of "the mountain rain is about to come." Then comes the torrential downpour, pattering crisply on the roofs of the attap houses. How clear and lovely this sound is, how poetic! At this time, if you wake up from a nap and listen to the crisp sound on the roof, you will be reminded of the poetic scene of listening quietly to the "sound of rain breaking the lotus sound" by the lotus pond at night.

After an hour or two, the wind and rain completely stop. The clouds clear, and the sky is bright. The sun is still embedded in the jade-like blue sky, peeking at people with a charming smile. At this time, everything on the earth appears extraordinarily fresh and peaceful. Then you drag your wooden clogs and walk alone to the suburbs, to the river to listen quietly to the gurgling water and to admire the crystal-clear water droplets on the lush green leaves, shining with golden light under the sunlight. At this time, you forget the heat of the weather in the South, and your heart will naturally feel infinitely pleasant and comfortable!

Every time I look at the annoying plum rain outside the window, it always makes me miss the pleasant rainy season in the South. However, the overseas Chinese, under multiple oppressions, have lost their past glory, and the world is no longer theirs!

This surging torrential rain of the South will henceforth be eternally buried in the depths of my heart!

Burial 260

— Lin Bin

Past life leaves only faint shadows on memory, like faded ancient paintings.

The faint shadows on these faded paintings are not shadows of people, flowers, or the moon, but rather shadows of smiles and traces of tears.

When people climb to the highest peak (whether it is the peak of happiness or the peak of pain), they always like to look back at the path where they have left their footprints. At this moment, as I am about to fall to the other side of life's peak, let me also look at the shadows of smiles and traces of tears left behind.

…In the hall, under the eaves, hung brilliant gauze lanterns. Candlelight shone through the red gauze, illuminating the hall full of banquets, the painting of the three stars in the center of the hall, the congratulatory screens with red background and golden characters on both sides, the bright red pillar couplets, and the bright red report card above the three stars, revealing the flat black characters on the report card: Your son ××× has completed his studies at this elementary school and passed the examination with satisfactory results and is hereby granted graduation…

"Congratulations, congratulations, in a few years he will be a foreign scholar!"

The short, stout father led his son, dressed in a new robe and jacket, into the hall, and all the red-faced guests in the hall stood up together.

…In a small thatched cottage in the green shade of the park. Ying and I held the poetry collection Golden Treasure and hummed famous love poems. The breeze blew the soft willow branches, rustling like whispers, like sighs. Sunlight passed through the gaps in the dense shade and fell on the rockery beside the pavilion, sometimes slipping here, sometimes slipping there, as if secretly watching our behavior and eavesdropping on our secrets.

"Ying, look! This sunlight is like a secret agent jointly dispatched by your father and my mother, spying on our actions."

"You are truly a cowardly animal, always associating everything with family obstacles. Have you forgotten the Shakespearean lines we just read? Love can penetrate rocks?"

"Can our love also penetrate rocks?"

"The question lies with you!"

Turning my face, my eyes met hers. One head slowly lowered, and the other followed closer.

…The sky was densely covered with hazy rain curtains, and the ground was dotted with small puddles. In the twilight of dusk, Ying and I were walking hurriedly.

"Are you really leaving me? Not caring about our two years of cohabitation?"

"It's not that I want to leave you, it's that life wants me to leave you."

"Can't life be changed?"

"Precisely because I want to change life, I am leaving you."

"Can't we change it together?"

"No. You want to drag me from the line of hunger to the line of death."

"Is there absolutely no way to save it? This is my last cry."

"No, this is the result of my half-year of consideration."

Stopping, watching Ying's shadow gradually disappear into the haze. … Dreaming, I returned to the pigeon-cage-like pavilion, took out my diploma from the bottom of the box, and tore it into countless small butterflies, scattering them on the floor.

…Inside the iron gate, the unique stench of the chicken coop.

I closed my eyes and immersed myself in meditation, thinking about life and death.

The iron gate clanged. My heart jumped. I opened my eyes. A hand handed me a Quaker bread wrapped in transparent white paper. "A woman sent it to you."

Taking it, I looked at it. On the white paper was a small square of white newspaper, which wrote: "I wish you good health! Ying."

In five minutes, I relived the past three years of my life. The corners of my eyes were a little wet.

Faint shadows of smiles and traces of tears! From now on, I will bury you in oblivion.

News Mr. Cui Wanqiu, after writing "New Road" and "Portraits of Women," has recently compiled his short stories from the years 1929 to 1934 and self-published a book titled "Red Dot," which includes ten stories: Duoga Zi, Red Dot, An Qi Sees It Disappear, The Drunkard's Intention, One Night at the Ballroom, The Cherry Blossoms are Gone, Song of the Migratory Birds, Drifting, and Disappointment. The first seven stories depict an extraordinary Japanese woman, sentimental and melancholic. The last three stories tell of the sorrow of middle-aged intellectuals, which are even more desolate and bleak. The first page includes a photograph of Duoga Zi, making it even more valuable. It is said that the general distribution is now handled by the Times Bookstore Company.

Shanghai Shenbao Local Supplement Film Special Issue

An Opinion for MGM after Garbo's "The Painted Veil" Failure 265

— Mizhen

Three months ago, a reporter from a major American newspaper predicted that Greta Garbo had reached a crossroads in her career. She had arrived at a very critical moment in her artistic life. Whether she could hold her position in the film industry would soon be revealed. If her "The Painted Veil" did not meet the expectations of the general American audience, she would have to take drastic measures to regain her original status.

Three months ago, the reporter also read the story of "The Painted Veil" and sighed for her. The story of "The Painted Veil" is based on the various threats and dangers encountered by white missionaries in Guangdong, China. It is indeed a film that insults our national identity and people. It depicts a severe epidemic raging in a certain county in Guangdong, with deaths all over the roads. Officials only knew how to pray to wooden puppets, and a large warehouse where the plague germs bred was not allowed to be burned. The missionary doctor then sacrificed himself to burn the warehouse, which led to him being threatened by local officials and gentlemen and falling into various dangers. It was written as if China was still like the extremely dark Africa.

At that time, when I saw this movie story, I sighed deeply. There were many reasons for my sigh, and of course, it was not just for Greta Garbo. I also sighed for MGM, the largest film company in the United States. I sighed for the superficial knowledge of foreigners among Americans. I also sighed for the friendship between China and the United States. When will the endless stream of anti-China films made by the United States come to an end? When will their perception of us improve? Do they not know, or do they deliberately choose not to know?

In order to shoot a film that takes scenery from a foreign country, major American companies do not hesitate to send large teams of people to London or Dublin to collect eighteenth-century clothing, supplies, and even trivial things like menus and wine bottles, and bring them back to Hollywood to ensure the authenticity of the film's content. Can't they send one or two people with clear eyes to come to the Chinese mainland to see if there is a place with a dense population where such a severe epidemic is raging, with deaths all over the roads, and officials and gentlemen only know how to pray to wooden puppets, and not a single doctor appears?

Three months ago, I knew that this kind of film would not come to China. I thought that if it did, it would be like being "not afraid of death," and we could express ourselves. If it didn't come, we would feel that we had no way to express ourselves. As expected, it did not come. Not only did it not come to China, but it also failed greatly in the United States. In the "Modern Screen" rating table, among many five-star blockbusters, it only received three stars, while the lowest still had two stars. The reason why it had one more star than the worst film was probably because of Garbo's reputation.

To be honest, in China, apart from the residual effects of some American publicity and occasional translations published in Chinese film magazines, we have never really worshipped Garbo. What we loved to watch in the past were Janet Gaynor, Norma Shearer, Loretta Young, and now Claudette Colbert, Myrna Loy, Loretta Young, Maureen O'Sullivan, etc. Although Garbo had moving performances in films such as "Romance" and "Queen Christina," the flaws did not outweigh the merits. We, perhaps because of her widow-like face, never felt very enthusiastic about her.

The decline of a movie star is regrettable, but after acting in a film that insults our national identity and race, we are just human beings, and according to the nature of the human race, we should be happy about it. But what responsibility should MGM, the company that produced this "anti-China film," bear? MGM's products have a very wide market in China, and they have a resident representative in Shanghai. I hope they can use this article to promote the attention of their domestic company authorities. Otherwise, even if the films they produce are not necessarily shown in China, in our sincere search for friendship with neighboring countries, even if they do not come, we will know and arouse strong resentment.

Film Reviews

Review of "Charlie Chan in Paris" 266

— Zong Han

Charlie Chan in Paris

—— Grand Theater

There are really too many Charlie Chan cases. In those films, Warner Oland's portrayal of the Chinese detective consistently uses ungrammatical English and sluggish movements to provide laughter. This cannot be said to be intentionally insulting Chinese people, but it always feels inappropriate to put such a personality on an intelligent detective. However, I cannot deny that Warner Oland has performing intelligence. It is not easy for an American to dress up as a Chinese person and grasp the typical expressions so that Chinese people also find it very similar. Therefore, Warner Oland can take credit for Charlie Chan cases being able to arouse the interest of the audience in China. In "Charlie Chan in Paris," most of his performances are no different from before. Once, when he got into the car, he naturally pulled the edge of the hat a few times, which imitated the posture of an old Chinese man and was indeed a typical performance.

The content of "Charlie Chan in Paris" is similar to previous Charlie Chan detective films or other detective films. It is nothing more than shady people plotting to kill for money. After Charlie Chan's detective work, the evildoers are brought to justice. At the same time, there will be no shortage of love between young men and women. The difference is that it shows a bank manager forging government bonds. Those who commit crimes are people in the upper class. After the manager's mask is revealed, it cannot but make the "gentlemen" shudder.

However, in terms of the image being presented, people will not be very complimentary. Generally speaking, the director is old-fashioned in learning the unique techniques commonly used in detective films, and there is nothing particularly commendable. The atmosphere in a few scenes is still very tight, such as the various scenes in the cellar. However, people have seen too many of these films, so they do not feel very interested, although the film itself is not a failure.

A recent photo of Ms. Yuan Shaomei, a newly promoted actress of Mingxing Film Company. Ms. Yuan has a profound performance in "Human Relations."

Review of "The Little Minister" 267

— You Jing

“The Little Minister”

— Grand Shanghai Theater

In the tide of "literary and artistic films," in addition to Dickens, Barrie (Sir James Matthew Barrie) is also a writer regarded as a money tree by producers. Not long ago, "What Every Woman Knows" was shown in Nanjing, and here is another "The Little Minister."

Due to the translation and introduction of several stage plays, Barrie is no longer a completely unfamiliar figure in the Chinese theater scene. He was born in Kirriemuir, Scotland, in 1860. After graduating from the University of Edinburgh at the age of twenty-two, he began to write manuscripts. In 1889, he gained prominence with his novel "A Window in Thrums," which expressed the life of Scottish farmers with strong local color, rich humor, fantasy, and humanitarian sympathy. Subsequently, he produced many novels, among which "The Little Minister" became one of his masterpieces, establishing his position in the literary world.

Like Galsworthy, Barrie was a novelist and playwright. Shortly after the release of "The Little Minister," he began writing various scripts, and by 1922, he had written as many as thirty-five plays. Among the most important are "The Admirable Crichton," "Peter Pan," "What Every Woman Knows," "Twelve Pound Look," and Dear Brutus, which Mr. Hong Shen read as "Second Dream." "The Little Minister" was also adapted into a script in 1897.

Barrie's plays have been highly praised by some drama critics of similar types, such as Barrett H. Clark and William Lyon Phelps. It is said that he summarizes the characteristics of contemporary allegorical playwrights. He has Galsworthy's keen understanding, Jones's moral sincerity, John Synge's deep passion, Dunsany's outstanding fantasy, Irvine's ethical logic, Shaw's extraordinary wisdom, and Pinero's technique. Naturally, we must admit these characteristics of Barrie. But when we still want to find something in his plays, we will feel that something is missing. He does not have Galsworthy's sense of justice, Shaw's hatred of evil, or the unequal cries of Yeats and Lady Gregory. Except for "The Twelve Pound Look," which is slightly related to the issue of couples, at most, it only stops at the utopian etiquette in "The Admirable Crichton."

In "What Every Woman Knows," Barrie touches on the fact that the petty bourgeoisie is climbing upwards with capitalism, but he emphasizes the expression in their male-female relationship; in "The Little Minister," he also moves from the life of the weavers who were slaughtered by the soldiers of the villainous shopkeeper colluding with the landlord in the burgeoning textile industry and the old poor woman Langley who was driven away by the landlord to the love affair between the minister and a woman. Is it not too fantastical that a woman of a despised Gypsy race would be so loved by a minister who is a teacher, even to the point where the feudal lord on whom he depends allows them to marry?

This "The Little Minister" film directed by Richard Wallace is quite remarkable in terms of technique. In the competition for literary and artistic films, the essential elements of elaborate production, from the selection of actors, background, and the authenticity of costumes and props, are not taken lightly.

Full of the simple flavor of the Scottish countryside, the passionate tears of the Gypsy girl, and the humorous ridicule, it is a clear and readable pastoral song, a lyrical short poem, a landscape sketch, and a quick sketch cartoon.

The performances of everyone in the cast are very average. Landell, who plays the drunk Roddy, Donald Crisp, who plays the doctor McQueen, Manley Gordon, who plays the old poor Langley, and the mother of the janitor, etc., are no less skilled than the two leading actors. Strictly speaking, the leading actress Katharine Hepburn is still able to give full play to the passionate and unrestrained personality that the Gypsy girl Babbie should have. John Beal, who plays the little minister, also has more solemn and calm demeanor, but lacks passionate and unrestrained performance.

Sun Shiyi Hired by Diantong 268

Since Diantong Company moved its factory and expanded its scale, it has not only strived for excellence in quality but also paid attention to mass production in quantity. In order to combat the trend of shoddy manufacturing on the one hand and save the current depression of the Chinese film industry on the other, it has now formed four directing teams and mobilized according to the entire plan. In addition to Xu Xingzhi's "Sons and Daughters in a Time of Storm," Situ Huimin's "Goddess of Freedom," and Yuan Muzhi's "Metropolitan Scenery," manager Ma Dejian, in order to strengthen his production plan, recently heard that Sun Shiyi had resigned from Lianhua, so he specially invited him to join. He has now been hired to serve as both director and chief screenwriter. In the future, he will focus on the production work of Diantong.

Film Novel

The Little Minister (IV) 269

— Zhi

But she knew that day. She heard a child crying in the praying grounds, begging her to leave this place, because people knew about her and the little minister. If she didn't leave, the little minister would be banished from the village. She then tearfully agreed to leave here forever. That night, she left a note with Langley for Gavin. Back at the castle, she urged the duke to marry her. In this sad mood, she even forgot about Langley. When her maid reminded her, she rushed to see her with money. She couldn't help but ask about Gavin's news. Langley told her: "These few days, I heard that Gavin is a little different from usual. Everyone in the village is paying attention to him. I heard it's because of a woman. Miss Babbie, it probably wouldn't be you, would it? He is a good minister... He's coming."

Babbie hurriedly hid in the house, secretly watching him through the small window. His ashen face made her feel her cruelty. She heard him say: "I really don't know what unfortunate things happened to her." At that time, the church bell rang, and he hurriedly said he was leaving: "This is a prayer meeting, I'm never late." But Langley deliberately asked him to move the spinning wheel into the house. This time, Babbie, hiding in the house, simply had nowhere to hide. Gavin then hugged her tightly and said: "Why did you leave me like this? You really don't know how sad I am." She could only explain: "There are some things I want to tell you..." "Tell me you love me, that's enough."

At first, Babbie hardened her heart and said that she was just playing with him, looking for fun. There was no other meaning. But when she looked at Gavin's disappointed look, she had to cry and say: "Oh! No, at first I was afraid so. Later, I really loved you. This is my fault. I shouldn't have done this, I shouldn't have embarrassed you and your mother." The little minister asked: "Do you really love me, and not the Duke of Lindores?" "Do you still ask me that?" "Then we'll go and talk to the duke. He will forgive you." Babbie shook her head and said: "It can't be done. You don't know him. He is very powerful, he will make everyone in the village oppose you." "Then I will defend myself. Aren't we in love? I can't give you up." As he said that, he was about to take her back to see his mother. But the crowd at the prayer meeting had to make him hurry back. He told her to go see his mother first.

Babbie arrived at his house. The one who opened the door for her was not Mrs. Gavin, but Jeannie. When Jeannie saw her, she reproachfully asked her that she shouldn't have caused the little minister to be banished from the church because of her. While Babbie was defending herself, Mrs. Gavin came down from upstairs. After she knew that Babbie was her son's lover, she not only didn't get angry, but also welcomed her and loved her. But what else did she know?

Babbie heard the noisy voices outside the door and knew that something was wrong. She immediately tried to get Mrs. Gavin upstairs. She herself went to open the door for the elders from the church. She sorrowfully begged them not to see Mrs. Gavin directly, at least to ask them to say it to her. Thomas shouted angrily: "Don't deny that he embraced you with his arms tonight. We all know." "No, you don't know." She said angrily, retreating: "Even if you know, it's not a bad thing. He wouldn't do such a thing, don't you know?" (To be continued)
